  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7148911c-d563-4a0e-acb3-bde6a480aaa0'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer12373929370303409664">"The body you are wearing used to be mine." So begins the letter Myfanwy Thomas is holding when she awakes in a London park surrounded by bodies all wearing latex gloves. With no recollection of who she is, Myfanwy must follow the instructions her former self left behind to discover her identity and track down the agents who want to destroy her.<br/><br/>She soon learns that she is </span>
  <span id="freeText12373929370303409664" style="display:none">"The body you are wearing used to be mine." So begins the letter Myfanwy Thomas is holding when she awakes in a London park surrounded by bodies all wearing latex gloves. With no recollection of who she is, Myfanwy must follow the instructions her former self left behind to discover her identity and track down the agents who want to destroy her.<br /><br />She soon learns that she is a Rook, a high-ranking member of a secret organization called the Chequy that battles the many supernatural forces at work in Britain. She also discovers that she possesses a rare, potentially deadly supernatural ability of her own. <br /><br />In her quest to uncover which member of the Chequy betrayed her and why, Myfanwy encounters a person with four bodies, an aristocratic woman who can enter her dreams, a secret training facility where children are transformed into deadly fighters, and a conspiracy more vast than she ever could have imagined.<br /><br />Filled with characters both fascinating and fantastical, <i>The Rook</i> is a richly inventive, suspenseful, and often wry thriller that marks an ambitious debut from a promising young writer.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12373929370303409664" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1711310780" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1711310780" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1711310780?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=paranormal-uf">paranormal-uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1711310780" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9203084791360697953"><blockquote>
  <i>“Yes, Minister, it turns out that there was a mysterious force that caused that plane to crash. We call it gravity.”</i>
</blockquote><br/>I can't believe no one has recommended - or even <i>mentioned</i> - this book to me before! It's a <b>creative, complex urban fantasy</b> with an hilarious and likable protagonist, monsters, and an intriguing mystery.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10836728.The_Rook__The_Checquy_Files___1_' title='The Rook (The Checquy Files, #1) by Daniel O'Malley' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Rook</a> grabbed me immediately. Myfanwy Thomas awakes surrounded by bodies with no recollection of who she is or what she's doing there. All she has is a letter in her pocket; </span>
  <span id="freeText9203084791360697953" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“Yes, Minister, it turns out that there was a mysterious force that caused that plane to crash. We call it gravity.”</i>
</blockquote><br />I can't believe no one has recommended - or even <i>mentioned</i> - this book to me before! It's a <b>creative, complex urban fantasy</b> with an hilarious and likable protagonist, monsters, and an intriguing mystery.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10836728.The_Rook__The_Checquy_Files___1_" title="The Rook (The Checquy Files, #1) by Daniel O'Malley" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rook</a> grabbed me immediately. Myfanwy Thomas awakes surrounded by bodies with no recollection of who she is or what she's doing there. All she has is a letter in her pocket; a letter that begins with <i>"The body you are wearing used to be mine."</i> She soon finds herself caught up in this life she never asked for, trying to figure out how she lost her memory, who's out to get her, and how to manage the basics of Myfanwy's job at the secret agency known as the <b>Checquy Group</b>.<br /><br />Just so you know: <b>there's a lot of infodump</b>. I usually don't like that, but it was fun enough here that I kept sprinting through pages anyway. The background of this world and the Checquy Group are revealed through letters that the former Myfanwy Thomas wrote before she lost her memory. These letters appear throughout the book and are, basically, witty infodumps. Still, I enjoyed them.<br /><br />Watching Myfanwy try to adjust to a life she doesn't remember is hilarious. And <b>she's kind of badass</b> - but not in the usual kicking ass way, more in a "I guess this shit is happening, but I'm still going to eat my Toblerone first" kind of way. My kinda girl.<br /><br />Turns out this Checquy Group is a secret organization that deals with all the supernatural nastiness in Britain. O'Malley gets a great balance between the humour and drama of Myfanwy's day-to-day life and relationships (no romance, though), and the greater mystery behind it. We all want answers to the big questions, but it was just as enjoyable to follow Myfanwy into the office.<br /><br />Some very weird and wonderful creatures exist in this world, and some of them are Myfanwy's colleagues. Like the creepy, awesome Rook Gestalt:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Three boys and one girl. Two of the boys were identical. That’s not the weirdest thing, however. The weirdest thing was that when all four pairs of eyes opened, only one mind was looking out from behind them. This was Gestalt.</i>
</blockquote><br />Then there's strong female friendships, snarking, and people who are willing to rip your face off first and ask questions later. <br /><br />Funny, compelling, and just the right amount of weird. <b>HELL YES.</b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“This should be a pleasant little interview. All I have to do is put on my scary face."<br />"You have a scary face?" Ingrid sounded skeptical.<br />"Yes," said Myfanwy indignantly. "I have a very scary face."<br />Ingrid surveyed her for a moment. "You may wish to take off the cardigan then, Rook Thomas," she advised tactfully. "The flowers on the pocket detract somewhat from your menace.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9203084791360697953" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_918635864" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/918635864" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/918635864?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=gender-bender">gender-bender</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=boarding-school">boarding-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=uk">uk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=twins-triplets-clones">twins-triplets-clones</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=kick-ass-heroine">kick-ass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=magic">magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer918635864" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10857276165277210230"><blockquote>
  <i>This is ridiculous, she thought. I’m possessed of terrifying powers. Why am I relying on a ridiculous little gun that I picked because I thought it was cute? I don’t need this thing. She threw it contemptuously over her shoulder.<br/><br/>There’s something foul wandering the underground tunnels beneath my office, something that’s invisible to my vaunted powers.<br/><br/>Crap.<br/><br/>Where’s my gun?</i>
</blockquote><b>This book is <i>X-Men</i> meets <i>X-Files</i> meets <i>The Bourne Identity</i> meets <i>Johnny English</i>.</b> And that may sound like a clusterfuck to e</span>
  <span id="freeText10857276165277210230" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>This is ridiculous, she thought. I’m possessed of terrifying powers. Why am I relying on a ridiculous little gun that I picked because I thought it was cute? I don’t need this thing. She threw it contemptuously over her shoulder.<br><br>There’s something foul wandering the underground tunnels beneath my office, something that’s invisible to my vaunted powers.<br><br>Crap.<br><br>Where’s my gun?</i>
</blockquote><b>This book is <i>X-Men</i> meets <i>X-Files</i> meets <i>The Bourne Identity</i> meets <i>Johnny English</i>.</b> And that may sound like a clusterfuck to end all clusterfucks, but somehow it works, or maybe my mind is just trying to make it better than it is because I'm coming off a massive chain of horrible books. Whatever. I loved it.<br><br>If this book were made into a movie, I can totally see Tina Fey in the lead role.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399525420i/9563163.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The good: <br><br>- Witty, dry, humorous writing<br>- <b>A female assassin/secret agent not afraid to kill</b>- A fun and interesting secret agency, think <b>"paranormal MI5"</b><br>- A well-executed <b>amnesia premise</b><br>- A racially diverse and fun suporting cast of characters<br>- <b>NO ROMANCE</b>. CAN I GET A FUCK, YEAH?!<br><br>The not so good:<br><br>- Questionable character development<br>- The length: it's a good book, but it could stand to be cut by a good 100 pages<br>- The infodump: It's a fun infodump, but it's still an infodump<br><br><u>The Summary</u>: <blockquote>
  <i>Dear You,<br>The body you are wearing used to be mine.</i>
</blockquote>A woman stood shivering in the rain, surrounded by a circle of dead bodies. She has no idea who she is. A letter inside her pocket informed her that she is a <b>Myfanwy Thomas</b>, pronounced <b>
  <i>miff-UN-nee</i>
</b>. The letter gives her instructions, where to go, what to do. She checks herself into a hotel, as instructed, finds more letters. The next morning, she leaves the hotel, and is promptly attacked by four people, one of them the receptionist.<br><br>Myfanwy's reaction is a little unexpected. She almost kills them.<blockquote>
  <i>When she opened her eyes and took a breath, she realized that there was no one holding her. Instead, the four people were lying on the ground, twitching uncontrollably.</i>
</blockquote>Interesting.<br><br><b>These letters will continue for the rest of the book.</b> They tell Myfanwy who she was, how she grew up, most importantly, they tell her that Myfanwy now works for a secret agency known as the <b>Checquy Group</b>. They've been in existence for hundreds of years, and Myfanwy is a Rook. One of the highest ranking members of the group. <b>Once you're in the Checquy Group, you don't get out.</b><blockquote>
  <i>I’ve only ever heard of three people who tried to leave the Checquy, and I know the history inside and out.<br>The first was a powered individual called Brennan the Intransigent who made a break for it in 1679. He was crucified on the cliffs of Dover.<br>The second was a soldier in 1802. He was carefully brought back to the Checquy stronghold and then buried alive in his village’s graveyard.<br>The third was a woman who could grow tentacles out of her back and exuded some sort of alarming toxin through her fingertips. Her stuffed body is currently displayed above the mantelpiece in one of the London offices.</i>
</blockquote>The Checquy Agency employs normal, loyal people, but the epistle of its powers lies in those with special powers, such as Myfanwy.<blockquote>
  <i>I gained the power to touch people and possess instant control of their bodies. I could make them move however I pleased. I could read their physical condition, detect pregnancy, cancer, a full bladder.</i>
</blockquote>Only, instead of being a super secret special agent, the old Myfanwy appears to be nothing more than a "glorified paper pusher," albeit a very powerful one. So what happened? <b>How did she lose her memories? Why did the old Myfanwy plan so carefully for such a scenario?</b><br><br>Lots of questions. Few answers. But for now, Myfanwy's still got a job to go to. She has to step into her former life without a beat, while avoiding her colleague's questions.<blockquote>
  <i>“Yes?” said Myfanwy. What, do these guys keep tabs on my comings and goings? “Well, I...had an appointment.” They regarded her with expectant eyes, and she was suddenly filled with a desire to shake up those proprietary stares. “A gynecologist appointment.” She smiled triumphantly at the twins. “To have my vagina checked.”</i>
</blockquote>And it has to be confessed that Myfanwy isn't altogether convincing at times.<blockquote>
  <i>“I’m sorry, Rook Thomas, but your car is here,” she said.<br>“My car?” Myfanwy said.<br>“It’s time for your dinner with Lady Farrier.”<br>“Oh, crap,” she sighed, then noticed Clovis’s shocked expression. “I mean, oh, good, this should be delightful.”</i>
</blockquote>There's a lot of weird crap thrown at her, including horrifying colleagues who wouldn't hesitate to literally rip someone's face off, and acquaintances who have been alive for thousands of years.<blockquote>
  <i>“… past century she is notable for having kneed Joseph Stalin in the groin during a drinks reception, and she played a large part in the South African diamond industry,” Ingrid went on. “She also cured one member of our royal family of cancer in the 1950s, and infected another with syphilis in the 1960s.”</i>
</blockquote>On her quest to find the truth about her memory loss, Myfanwy will face terrifying danger, manipulative colleagues, plagues, vampires, werewolves, mold monsters, and company parties.<blockquote>
  <i>I can’t wear this!” Myfanwy exclaimed in horror.<br>“You can’t wear that!” the housekeeper exclaimed.<br>“It’s like all the material that’s supposed to be on top migrated to the bottom,” said Val.<br>Any wedding in which this dress appeared on the bride would have to be pretty damn open-minded, thought Myfanwy. And might well incorporate the honeymoon on the altar.</i>
</blockquote><u>The Setting</u>: This book is an infodump. I usually hate infodumping, but it was done exceedingly well in this book. <b>Through a series of letters, the old Myfanwy explained the inner workings, the history, and the stories surrounding the infernal Checquy Agency.</b> It's a pretty typical paranormal agency, but it is so well-presented, from the internal politics, to the ranking, to the little-known details only an insider would know. It's an old agency, it is resistant to change. Paranormal or not, some things remain the same.<blockquote>
  <i>Occasionally, someone will point out these flaws and attempt to institute a change, but that person is slapped down. The reasons for this down-slappage are:<br><br>If you’re in the Court, you have an impressive title, and you don’t want to change it for something generic.<br><br>Tradition.<br><br>It’s supposed to remind us of the importance of strategy and of rank.<br><br>It’s cool.</i>
</blockquote>The premise of the superpowers are similar to that of the X-Men. While most of them lack the extent of the full mutant appearance, the players within the Checquy Agency are quite dangerous and abnormal. Like the fabulously Children-of-the-Corn Rook Gestalt.<blockquote>
  <i>Three boys and one girl. Two of the boys were identical. That’s not the weirdest thing, however. The weirdest thing was that when all four pairs of eyes opened, only one mind was looking out from behind them. This was Gestalt.<br><br>Gestalt is kind of disconcerting, because it/he/she/they is/are spread over four bodies.</i>
</blockquote><b>f you wanted people with freakishly awesome powers who aren't afraid to use said power to maim, torture, and kill, you won't do much better than this book.</b><br><br><u>Myfanwy</u>:<br><br>The good:<br><br>- <b>She is hilariously average</b>. She is quite plain in appearance (and no, nobody falls in love with her), her body is nothing special. She has terrible taste in clothing. She likes bunnies. She loves Toblerone chocolate. She has a tendency to stumble. While the old Myfanwy was a wallflower, the new Myfanwy is more apt to put her foot in her mouth, with a preference to run and hide rather than do anything heroic. But she can't, because she's a powerful person without being able to remember it. Crap.<br><br>She is jealous sometimes while never, ever slut shaming or hating another female for her appearance. In fact, one of the women with whom she works.<blockquote>
  <i>Please let her have slept her way to the top, thought Myfanwy. No one deserves to be this beautiful and clever too.</i>
</blockquote>Turns out to be not only beautiful, but awesome, nice, and a great friend.<br><br>- <b>She is super super super deadly</b>, and is kind of a special snowflake at times.<blockquote>
  <i>My God, you were the most exciting find in decades! All of us knew about your potential. The tutors at the Estate were babbling about you to everyone!”</i>
</blockquote>But it doesn't piss me off because she doesn't really give a fuck. The old Myfanwy is scared, she chokes, she hates using her powers to harm. The new Myfanwy doesn't have those reservations, but she's still not inclined to get into dangerous situations because 1. She doesn't want to, and 2. She really doesn't have a clue what's going on most of the time.<br><br>- <b>Blending in</b>: When you're an amnesiac, trying to get back into the swing of things at your paranormal MI5 workplace is kind of hard, especially when you have multiple-body-psychic-colleagues. I mean, what are you supposed to do when they're mentally killing something in front of you?<blockquote>
  <i>Finally, after a high-pitched kiYAA!, they settled back, breathing heavily, and explained that Eliza had just broken the neck of the leader of the antler cult, and that the complex was secured.<br>“Wow. Great,” said Myfanwy. “Nicely done.”<br>“Hmm,” said Tidy Twin absently. “Eliza has blood on her boots.”<br>“That’s lovely, Gestalt,” Myfanwy said, trying to keep her cool. “More coffee? Or more orange juice? No? Perhaps I could have Ingrid fetch you a couple of moist towelettes.”</i>
</blockquote><b>The Not-So-Good</b>: Really, there's only one thing. Her personality change. She has amnesia, and as mentioned, Myfanwy has trouble trying to get back into things and appearing normal. She's clumsy, but sometimes, she is far, far too competent and take-charge very early on when she largely hasn't a fucking clue of what's going on. Like during her first meeting, when things get out of hand, Myfanwy decides to take charge.<blockquote>
  <i>“Gentlemen!” she finally shouted, and her voice cut through the noise like a scythe through a poodle. There was dead silence, and everyone stared at her, stunned. “You all need to shut up and stay focused on the task at hand. Dr. Crisp, if you will turn your eyes back toward the interrogation, I wonder if you could revive the subject and question him.”</i>
</blockquote>This is entirely too confident, too much for me to believe. I can understand a personality change, but I can't accept that Myfanwy can be so utterly silly and incompetent-sounding on one page, while being competely take-charge in the next.<br><br><u>The Writing</u>: <blockquote>
  <i>It was an old room in an old building and was decorated in a very specific style that showed the decorators were lacking both imagination and a second X chromosome.</i>
</blockquote>It's hilarious, but it's not like ha-ha hilarious. <b>The author is American, but he does a damn fine job of replicating dry, deprecating British wit</b>.<br><br><u>The Romance</u>: THERE IS NONE! HALLELUJAH!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10857276165277210230" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1190439772956131120"><b>Audio re/read so I can carry on with the next book. There are too many next books I need to get read!</b><br/><br/>I freaking loved this book! <br/><br/><img alt=' ' src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469456666ra/19819992.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I can't believe this was the author's first book =) It's got all kinds of cray, some ewww, some funny parts. Well, I almost peed my pants at times but I digress.<br/><br/>Myfanwy Thomas, known as Rook Thomas, wakes up not knowing who she is. There are dead bodies all around. There is a note in her pocket and lots of instructions and letters through-out the book. Rook Thomas has </span>
  <span id="freeText1190439772956131120" style="display:none"><b>Audio re/read so I can carry on with the next book. There are too many next books I need to get read!</b><br><br>I freaking loved this book! <br><br><img alt=" " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469456666ra/19819992.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I can't believe this was the author's first book =) It's got all kinds of cray, some ewww, some funny parts. Well, I almost peed my pants at times but I digress.<br><br>Myfanwy Thomas, known as Rook Thomas, wakes up not knowing who she is. There are dead bodies all around. There is a note in her pocket and lots of instructions and letters through-out the book. Rook Thomas has powers along with all kinds of creatures do that her form of government work to oversee so to speak. <br><br>I'm still confused as to whether Rook Thomas was before and was she after &lt; --- only people that have read the book will know what I'm talking about. Maye =D <br><br>And then there is Rook Gesalt! Wasn't it great fun. I will let you all meet it for yourself. <br><br>God, I freaking loved Myfanwy and Shantay together. Shantay came over from America when Myfanwy's group found out some stuff from this person they had captured. The group was going to torture him and some stuff went down and freaked everyone out. <br><br>But oh, the girls had the best time. I almost cracked a rib laughing when they went into this place together to see what kind of freaky thing was causing chaos. I wish I could excerpt the whole thing! <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>Poppat gripped her arm desperately. "Myfanwy, we both know this is not your field. I can't let you go in there alone."<br><br>"No" came a firm voice from behind them. They turned to see Shantay zipping herself into a Pawn combat uniform. She'd coiled her hair up at the back of her neck and suddenly looked much more dangerous. "She's not going in alone. I'm going in with her."<br><br>"Absolutely not," said Mayfanwy. "There may be legal precedents for you coming along to observe, but can you imagine the repercussions if a Bishop of the Croatoan was harmed on a Checquy op?"<br><br>"Yeah, but you'll probably be dead too, so it's not like it'll be your problem." <br><br>"Well, then," said Myfanwy. "As long it causes me no inconvenience."</blockquote>
</b><br><br>When they got inside I about peed myself. I felt like I was reading a weird version of Stephanie and Lula (only Plum series lovers will get that reference) <br><br>Anyway, I had loads of fun and am going to be getting my next book as soon as BN sends me my reward card =) <br><br>Enjoy! <br><br>Mel ♥</span>

<div id="review_318224515" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/318224515" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/318224515?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who like all those movies I mentioned</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=female-lead">female-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=my-library-kindle">my-library-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=to-buy-hardcover">to-buy-hardcover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=fast-and-fun">fast-and-fun</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer318224515" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5188547601138758298">Finally! First great read of the year. Admittedly, that's because I'm hoarding <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12812550.Days_of_Blood___Starlight__Daughter_of_Smoke___Bone___2_' title='Days of Blood & Starlight (Daughter of Smoke & Bone, #2) by Laini Taylor' rel='nofollow noopener'>Days of Blood & Starlight</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13538708.The_Girl_Who_Fell_Beneath_Fairyland_and_Led_the_Revels_There__Fairyland___2_' title='The Girl Who Fell Beneath Fairyland and Led the Revels There (Fairyland, #2) by Catherynne M. Valente' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Girl Who Fell Beneath Fairyland and Led the Revels There</a> like a survivalist with canned goods, or a chocoholic with a secret stash of Toblerone in the back of the freezer (not that I'm speaking from experience). And while I tempered down my five stars to a more reasonable four, the fact is this was a perfect read the first time through. <br/><br/>I'll save the detailed summary; this is one time</span>
  <span id="freeText5188547601138758298" style="display:none">Finally! First great read of the year. Admittedly, that's because I'm hoarding <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12812550.Days_of_Blood___Starlight__Daughter_of_Smoke___Bone___2_" title="Days of Blood &amp; Starlight (Daughter of Smoke &amp; Bone, #2) by Laini Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">Days of Blood &amp; Starlight</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13538708.The_Girl_Who_Fell_Beneath_Fairyland_and_Led_the_Revels_There__Fairyland___2_" title="The Girl Who Fell Beneath Fairyland and Led the Revels There (Fairyland, #2) by Catherynne M. Valente" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl Who Fell Beneath Fairyland and Led the Revels There</a> like a survivalist with canned goods, or a chocoholic with a secret stash of Toblerone in the back of the freezer (not that I'm speaking from experience). And while I tempered down my five stars to a more reasonable four, the fact is this was a perfect read the first time through. <br /><br />I'll save the detailed summary; this is one time when the blurb gets it right. It starts rather hard-core action movie: woman coming to consciousness in a midst of a circle of bodies, no memory of self or events, dripping from the rain and blood. She discovers an envelope in her pocket from the Myfanwy-That-Was. Soon it evolves into a James Bond-style government agency spy thriller crunched with identity disorientation of <i>The Bourne Identity.</i> Halfway through I realize O'Malley is channeling <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11.The_Hitchhiker_s_Guide_to_the_Galaxy__Hitchhiker_s_Guide_to_the_Galaxy___1_" title="The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy (Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy, #1) by Douglas Adams" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy</a>, or at least <i>Men In Black,</i> and that the flashbacks felt a lot like <i>X-Men.</i> (I'm finding it disturbing that I'm describing a book by referencing movies. Is that acceptable in a book review?)<br /><br />Narrative shifts between letters from Myfanwy-That-Was to the current scramble of Myfanwy-That-Is to solve the mystery of who is trying to kill her. While that had the potential to become a tiresome device, O'Malley uses it well, giving context to Newbie just before she needs to use it, cuing the reader at the same time. Sometimes Senior relates an incident, sometimes she lays out structure and organization, or gives a dossier on other characters. For the most part it was able to maintain pace and tension through the shifts. At times, O'Malley is tongue-in-cheek: right as Myfanwy thinks, "I suppose I should do some more homework on how this organization actually works," the next section is from one of the letters, under the title of "How This Organization Actually Works." I actually found it rather delightful, highlighting the mental similarities in how they process information. <br /><br />As the story develops, Myfanwy starts to take on her own personality, more abrupt and direct than the prior, who she now thinks of as "Thomas," their last name. I thought the transition between the two was handled well, and as the story developed, I cared just as much about what happened to Thomas and wanted to know her story, even though I knew where it would end (here's where my habit of peeking at the end of books comes in handy; it's kind of like the book is a spoiler for it's own self because we know Thomas is 'dead,' or at least, gone). I enjoyed Myfanwy's character breaks, and it set the stage for gentle humor as she responded almost--but not quite--in character: <b><br />"An emergency has emerged, and both you and Rook Gestalt have been summoned to an interrogation," the secretary replied in an unruffled manner.<br />"Oh. Okay." Myfanwy looked down and her desk, thought for a moment, and then looked up. "Are we getting interrogated, or are we doing the interrogating?" she asked.<br /></b><br />Then there is:<b><br />"It's time for your dinner with Lady Farrier."<br />"Oh, crap," she sighed, then noticed Clovis's shocked expression. "I mean, oh, good, this should be delightful."<br /></b><br />The humor isn't out front in the beginning, which now strikes me as one of the delightful parts about the writing. Tightly wound around an action core at the start, O'Malley sneaks in humor one subtle comment at a time, gradually becoming more absurd. The first hint that we aren't in London any more comes about three chapters in when we meet Rook Gestalt, really one of the more innovative creations in sci-fi/fantasy literature that I've happened upon. One mind, four bodies. I found myself trying to wrap my head around that one (somewhat distracted by comparing it with Zaphod and his two heads) and just got rather smacked with the possibilities. By the end, the absurd veered out of control at a couple of points, but for the most part O'Malley was able to maintain the balance between chuckles and tension. <br /><br />Before too long, the American version of the Court comes to call, and the subtlety gloves come off when the American Bishop Shantay and Myfanwy take on some fungus--after lunch, of course.<br /><b><br />"'That is experience talking,' said Shantay. 'In these situations the glass is always half-empty.'<br />'Always?'<br />'Always,' confirmed the Bishop. 'Right until it fills up with some sort of spectral blood that grows into a demon entity.' <br /></b><br />Or a threat:<br /><b><br />'I'll kill you first,' promised Myfanwy in a cold voice. 'I'll kill you twice if I feel like it.'<br /></b><br />Truly riveting fun, exactly what I needed after an awful start to the week--it was the ideal book experience of immersion and diversion. Highly recommended to anyone who likes a dose of humor with their surreal action-spy-mystery thriller.<br /><br />Four out of five stars. Or are they?<br /><br /><br />Update from Dec. 2015 re:read: I think I nailed it fairly well the first time, except that part about humor. It's seriously funny almost all the way through, in that very British way.<br />Cross posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2013/02/13/the-rook-by-daniel-omalley-or-the-first-great-read-of-2013/">http://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2013/0...</a><br /><br />Update from September 2019: idk 'almost all the way through.' There is a lot of back story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5188547601138758298" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_411759697" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/411759697" />
    <a title="mark monday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday"><img alt="mark monday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572672245p2/131922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/411759697?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mark monday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mark monday" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday">mark monday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=secret-histories">secret-histories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer411759697" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5939716010240226752">page turner, page turner! lady wakes in park with no memory! battered & bruised & bloody! surrounded by dead people! that she killed with her bare hands! cause she has special powers! the same special powers that i have often imagined myself having if dreams came true! quelle coincidence!<br/><br/>the narrative is propulsive. the ideas are automatically right up my alley. the whole thing is clearly built for fun; i gave it to a colleague and he immediately halted the book he was reading because the jacket</span>
  <span id="freeText5939716010240226752" style="display:none">page turner, page turner! lady wakes in park with no memory! battered &amp; bruised &amp; bloody! surrounded by dead people! that she killed with her bare hands! cause she has special powers! the same special powers that i have often imagined myself having if dreams came true! quelle coincidence!<br /><br />the narrative is propulsive. the ideas are automatically right up my alley. the whole thing is clearly built for fun; i gave it to a colleague and he immediately halted the book he was reading because the jacket description alone was enough to give him a massive boner. same here. but... i could have been challenged or surprised a bit more. the narrative goes back and forth between the present day actions of the woman before us and past letters that the woman she used to be wrote to her - which could have opened up many interesting possibilities. not even necessarily <i>literary</i> possibilities but maybe something along the lines of a potboiler-cum-meditation-on-memory like Memento. but nope, all those letters from the past serve a very straightforward function: infodumps. hella infodumps. entertaining and intriguing infodumps, and nothing more.<br /><br />but... page turner, page turner! young woman is named Miffanwy, rhymes with Tiffany! she works for a secret government agency that is staffed by people with super powers and whose goal is to protect the world from super-powered and supernatural threats! including the evil Belgian Grafters! the high-level administrators have titles named after chess pieces! cool! my favorite is one who lives in multiple bodies and whose name is Gestalt! Miffanwy is in charge of domestic operations and her title is The Rook!<br /><br />you know what i hate? well, many things, but in this instance the answer would be <i>cheap snarkiness</i>. ugh, i even hate the word. "snarky"... such an ugly word, like it was made up by a 12-year old. the only cheap snarkiness i appreciate is the kind that pops out of my mouth or from my keyboard; otherwise, it needs to be good or the eye-rolling will commence. Good as in the films of Howard Hawks. or Joss Whedon, some of the time. unfortunately, most snark is of the CW or SyFy networks variety, which to me is just lazy, shallow writing. unfortunately this novel is full of cheap snarky dialogue that comes out of nearly every character (that is when they are not sounding like The Lord and Lady of The Masterpiece Theater Manor). and so characters end up sounding just like each other and as if they just stepped out of one of the Scream films. it grew tedious. and hey, Daniel O'Malley, listen: high-level government administrators in both the U.S. and the U.K., particularly ones who are women, probably do not refer to other women as "chicks" on a regular basis. now that was just intolerable to read.<br /><br />but... page turner, page turner! ignore the bitching above! this book was all kinds of fun and i read it like reading was going to be declared illegal at the end of the night! pure pleasure! i can't wait for the sequel! plus no tedious romance to speak of! yay! woot! win!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5939716010240226752" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_283345838" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/283345838" />
    <a title="Amy Warrick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5900066-amy-warrick"><img alt="Amy Warrick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311870137p2/5900066.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/283345838?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy Warrick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy Warrick" href="/user/show/5900066-amy-warrick">Amy Warrick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer283345838" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13361156222170974577"><br/> I tried to like this book, I really did. I have disliked so many books lately that I am afraid of becoming a book curmudgeon. But this book deserved my dislike - it ASKED for my dislike. <br/><br/> This book reads like the beloved project of the geeky high school junior who has been told by too many English teachers that he has talent and should be a WRITER. What little action takes place, does so between enormous wads of italic description. You know how you've read books in which a character finds lette</span>
  <span id="freeText13361156222170974577" style="display:none"><br /> I tried to like this book, I really did. I have disliked so many books lately that I am afraid of becoming a book curmudgeon. But this book deserved my dislike - it ASKED for my dislike. <br /><br /> This book reads like the beloved project of the geeky high school junior who has been told by too many English teachers that he has talent and should be a WRITER. What little action takes place, does so between enormous wads of italic description. You know how you've read books in which a character finds letters left behind, that help her figure out what's going on? Imagine a suitcase full of letters. Imagine a fictional world that is so weak and spindly it needs pages of explanation to keep it going. <br /> <br /> Imagine an amnesiac taking the helm of a major international organization and nobody being the wiser. Imagine high school humor masquerading as clever. Imagine an interesting premise bludgeoned to death by its own ego. <br /><br /> Imagine yourself reading a different book. I did, and put this one down before the halfway point. <br /> <br /> Gosh, this is a bit negative, isn't it. </span>

<div id="review_836072199" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/836072199" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/836072199?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=all-aboard-the-superpowers-train">all-aboard-the-superpowers-train</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer836072199" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3865565731758778672"><b>$2.99 Kindle sale, July 14, 2019.</b> Loved it! Review posted at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com'>www.fantasyliterature.com:</a><br/><br/>As Daniel O’Malley’s supernatural thriller <i>The Rook</i> (book one of THE CHECQUY FILES) begins, Myfanwy Thomas comes to herself with complete amnesia. She’s standing in a London park at night. Surrounding her is a ring of motionless bodies. They are all wearing latex gloves.<br/><br/>Myfanwy (“rhymes with Tiffany”) finds two letters in her jacket pocket from her former self:<blockquote>
  <i>Dear You, The body you are wearing used to be m</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText3865565731758778672" style="display:none"><b>$2.99 Kindle sale, July 14, 2019.</b> Loved it! Review posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com">www.fantasyliterature.com:</a><br /><br />As Daniel O’Malley’s supernatural thriller <i>The Rook</i> (book one of THE CHECQUY FILES) begins, Myfanwy Thomas comes to herself with complete amnesia. She’s standing in a London park at night. Surrounding her is a ring of motionless bodies. They are all wearing latex gloves.<br /><br />Myfanwy (“rhymes with Tiffany”) finds two letters in her jacket pocket from her former self:<blockquote>
  <i>Dear You, The body you are wearing used to be mine… I’m writing this letter for you to read in the future.</i>
</blockquote>Myfanwy’s former self was aware that in some way her brain was going to be magically wiped of all memories, and did her best to smooth the way for future memory-less Myfanwy by writing a number of letters to herself.<blockquote>
  <i>All you need to know immediately is that someone I should be able to trust has decided that I need to be removed. I don’t know exactly who. I don’t know why. It may be for something I haven’t even done yet.</i>
</blockquote>The second letter presents her with a choice: go into hiding for the rest of her life, using the fortune in a bank account specified in the letter, or jump back into her prior life and try to find out why she was betrayed.<br /><br />New Myfanwy fully intends to grab the money and take off, but another attempted assassination convinces her that the only feasible option is to stay and fight. Having selected Option #2, she (and we) embark on reading a long series of letters from her former self, which explain Myfanwy’s past life as a high-ranking member of the Checquy, an organization of people with superpowers who help Great Britain and the world with various types of supernatural threats. It’s sort of like the X-men, except with a lot more British bureaucracy. Myfanwy needs to figure out who in the Checquy betrayed her and why, while trying to hide from everyone the fact that she no longer remembers anyone or anything.<br /><br />As an info-dumping device, the letters are a bit transparent, but it’s all interesting enough that I never felt like complaining… except for one or two times when these flashback letters interrupted a particularly suspenseful scene. First get Myfanwy out of mortal danger, THEN give us another letter!<br /><br />In an interesting conceit, the Checquy organization is based upon chess pieces: there’s a Lord and a Lady (the king and queen of the organization), two Bishops, two Rooks, etc. Only those people who have some kind of supernatural power can be in the top ranks of the Checquy. All others are Pawns — which leads to some understandable resentments and tensions in the ranks. Also, it quickly becomes apparent that former Myfanwy, for certain reasons in her past, was an extremely sensitive and timid person and, despite her stellar organizational skills, was not much respected within the Checquy. New Myfanwy, not burdened by those painful memories, soon starts to spread her wings and exercise her clout within the organization.<br /><br />There are multiple types of superpowers on display in <i>The Rook</i>, but they’re not your run-of-the-mill superpowers. We have, for example, Gestalt, who is a single mind that inhabits four very good-looking and frequently homicidal bodies. Others can exude poisonous clouds of ink, sprout quills, or develop an impenetrable steel coating.<br /><br /><i>The Rook</i> is written in a breezy, easy-to-read style, with a lot of wry humor in the writing and dialogue. There are several laugh-out-loud moments:<blockquote>It was a dress designed to draw attention. “You look like Cinderella,” said Val in awe.<br /><br />“Yeah, if she’d been into bondage and had Christian Dior as a godmother.”</blockquote>Myfanwy is an easy protagonist to root for as, despite the handicap of her memory loss, she gamely takes on both her coworkers in the Checquy as well as the enemies they’re battling. After the initial set-up there’s a lot of action in the plot… except when it’s slowed down by the ubiquitous letters from Myfanwy’s former self. The mystery of Myfanwy’s secret enemy kept the plot suspenseful, and there were some interesting twists that I didn’t foresee.<br /><br /><i>The Rook</i> may not be Great Literature, but it was just so much fun!<br /><br />4.5 stars.<br /><br />Content advisory: scattered F-bombs; a fair amount of violence and gore.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3865565731758778672" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9202327334326406582">I mean, I loved this book. Myfanwy Thomas wakes up with a note that says, "This body used to be mine". YEAH! I LOVE AMNESIA PLOTS! Except this is a bit more than that. Secret societies are kind of my fave, and this book builds a GREAT one. The secret Chequey (I love all the chess terms) battle supernatural forces in the world, and this new amnesiac is now fully immersed in it. I definitely felt like this could be a TV show, the richness of the world is so good! The tone is a bit hard to grasp, b</span>
  <span id="freeText9202327334326406582" style="display:none">I mean, I loved this book. Myfanwy Thomas wakes up with a note that says, "This body used to be mine". YEAH! I LOVE AMNESIA PLOTS! Except this is a bit more than that. Secret societies are kind of my fave, and this book builds a GREAT one. The secret Chequey (I love all the chess terms) battle supernatural forces in the world, and this new amnesiac is now fully immersed in it. I definitely felt like this could be a TV show, the richness of the world is so good! The tone is a bit hard to grasp, but it's classic British "serious but also cheeky", so once you get on the tricycle you're golden. It's just FUN, like Dr. Who.<br /><br />The pacing of this book was the only part I can quibble with, a bit erratic at times, but the world building was rich and the characters super fun, I loved it and would like to see more in the world!<br /></span>

<div id="review_261401954" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/261401954" />
    <a title="Cy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4833544-cy"><img alt="Cy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338977115p2/4833544.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/261401954?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cy" href="/user/show/4833544-cy">Cy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer261401954" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10349815541013580912">Honest to god, I'm both confused that I'm still reading this book and appalled at how highly rated it seems to be everywhere. The praise this book has been getting got me interested in reading it, and within a few chapters I had to wonder if there was some massive conspiracy...<br/><br/>To put it quite simply, the book has an intriguing premise that's destroyed by a hackneyed writing style, a juvenile approach to character, and a narrative that is grossly overshadowed by the writer's apparently high opini</span>
  <span id="freeText10349815541013580912" style="display:none">Honest to god, I'm both confused that I'm still reading this book and appalled at how highly rated it seems to be everywhere. The praise this book has been getting got me interested in reading it, and within a few chapters I had to wonder if there was some massive conspiracy...<br /><br />To put it quite simply, the book has an intriguing premise that's destroyed by a hackneyed writing style, a juvenile approach to character, and a narrative that is grossly overshadowed by the writer's apparently high opinion of his own talents. <br /><br />The main character is not even remotely likeable. When she's not being a high school prom queen (regularly calling technical people "nerds"; repeatedly criticizing the dress sense of the former occupant of her body), she's delivering "oh snap" wisecracks. She's just strong enough to take command of a situation when a story needs it, but also nicely "feminine" enough to need to be rescued. She confronts the leader of the enemy forces and her primary concern is the gross goop getting on her clothes. She appears commanding and independent, and in the next scene is naked in front of a stranger for laughs and then subjected to intrusive and demeaning physical exams for more comedy. She's strong-willed enough to be attractive, but not so much that she's truly an independent character. Her sexuality is regularly, and offensively, used as a tool to humiliate her for laughs, and that makes her non-threatening. In short, she's not a character so much as she's a collection of tropes designed to make her the perfect female character for the male audience.<br /><br />To make matters worse, none of the secondary characters are anything more than one to two word tropes. Ingrid: motherly secretary, Shantay: sassy friend, Alrich: mysterious vampire, etc. None of these characters develop from these descriptions into anything memorable.<br /><br />Setting aside the issue with characters is the issue with plot: Myfanwy goes from knowing absolutely nothing to be a confident and controlled leader of a powerful government organization? How much time has passed between her waking up and her turning into this bombshell in a suit? We're told it's been several weeks and it's here that we arrive at the crux of the problem with the narrative: we're told too much. We're told everything. We're not left to learn anything. Practically overnight, she turns from this terrified mouse whose every third thought is "DO THEY KNOW MY SECRET?!" to this confident administrator. When her sister appears, we're told, suddenly, that she is lonely and wants friends and family. There's no buildup. There's no sense of this given to the reader through dialogue and emotional description. I had no idea this was coming. We're told that she suddenly wants to be with friends and family, just as we're told that she becomes confident in her new role. These are just two examples of many.<br /><br />This goes further than just the author hamfistedly handing us important facts about the characters as though we're moving our way down a checklist. The book redefines what it means to infodump. Nearly every chapter is interrupted by what is essentially an encyclopedia entry giving us the history of the character Myfanwy just met or the term she just encountered. When it's not an infodump about a character, it's a letter written by the pre-amnesia Myfanwy telling the current Myfanwy some story that is rarely connected with the plot at hand, and it's usually written in such exacting, narrative detail that violates the nature of the epistolary format that these sections are written in. <br /><br />Finally, there are just so many parts of the plot that make ABSOLUTELY NO SENSE: you're hunted by the same person who made you lose your memory and just killed a bunch of your friends and you decide to go out clubbing? (and then the author spends four pages talking about how ruined her clothes were and her struggles to get her car back from a hotel garage). In what world would this be even slightly logical? <br /><br />An unequivocally awful book. Avoid, unless you're looking for something for kindling.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10349815541013580912" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1590089703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9968055385457948612"><b>Sale Alert: Oct 13, 2019 Kindle Deal for <a href='https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B004QX07EG/ref=s9_acsd_hps_bw_c_x_5_w?pf_rd_m=ATVPDKIKX0DER&pf_rd_s=merchandised-search-2&pf_rd_r=12PMX0SXGR7TJQ9W6X0P&pf_rd_t=101&pf_rd_p=efbd074c-33ab-4b82-9b90-7265f897ce5d&pf_rd_i=11552285011' rel='nofollow noopener'>$3.99</a></b><br/><br/><b>You’ve woken up and are surrounded by a handful of dead people wearing gloves and have no idea who you are or how you got there. </b> But luckily there is a note and with this note and a few others you learn about a world you had no idea even existed.<br/><blockquote>
  <i>Dear You, <br/>The odds of your reading this are slim to none. Who would choose uncertainty and vaguely worded warnings over a new life of wealth and luxury? I can only assume that you were put under a massive</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText9968055385457948612" style="display:none"><b>Sale Alert: Oct 13, 2019 Kindle Deal for <a href="https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B004QX07EG/ref=s9_acsd_hps_bw_c_x_5_w?pf_rd_m=ATVPDKIKX0DER&amp;pf_rd_s=merchandised-search-2&amp;pf_rd_r=12PMX0SXGR7TJQ9W6X0P&amp;pf_rd_t=101&amp;pf_rd_p=efbd074c-33ab-4b82-9b90-7265f897ce5d&amp;pf_rd_i=11552285011" rel="nofollow noopener">$3.99</a></b><br /><br /><b>You’ve woken up and are surrounded by a handful of dead people wearing gloves and have no idea who you are or how you got there. </b> But luckily there is a note and with this note and a few others you learn about a world you had no idea even existed.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Dear You, <br />The odds of your reading this are slim to none. Who would choose uncertainty and vaguely worded warnings over a new life of wealth and luxury? I can only assume that you were put under a massive amount of stress, touched someone’s skin, and they were paralyzed. Or blinded. Or lost the ability to speak. Or befouled themselves. Or one of several other effects that I won’t outline right now.</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>Well the good news is that at least you woke up awesome with some kind of superpower.</b> The bad news is that you now have to impersonate someone you have never met, figure out what happened to you and who is probably trying to kill you…since whoever ‘they’ are they don’t seem to have any idea that you are no longer her.<br /><br />Confusing? Nah, not really. What it is IS a wonderful set up to a completely interesting idea. <b> Myfanwy (the W is silent) Thomas is going to pretend to be a member of a super-secret government agency that deals with supernatural and paranormal situations and disturbances.</b> She is going to try and figure out who tried to have her killed and why, just as soon as she figures out how to be Myfanwy Thomas.<br /><br />I enjoyed a very large section of the story because I found it fascinating on quite a few levels. But, since I read this in a group there were varied opinions on the layout of the story and I will say that while it didn’t bother me it did bother a few of them. See there is a lot of infodumping. But I’m going to give it a pass because of the way it was presented. Thomas wrote letters to herself after a psychic told her she would lose all her memories and in those is where we get a lot of history to the Checquy (Her Majesty’s Supernatural Secret Service) and Thomas’s position in it. <b>Not every letter ends up being pertinent to the story because how was Thomas supposed to know and sometimes I think it reads a lot like a journal of someone’s day.</b> So while I liked this aspect of the story because of the extra details and such I think others got bored with it since some of it had nothing to do with the story. <b>I was completely entertained and so I will allow it. </b><br /><br />For me this is a great blend of humor and Urban Fantasy. Myfanwy is easy to like and I enjoyed even the times she is fumbling through her life. Seeing this world around her as she discovers everything that you never knew existed was a fantastic tale and I really wanted to get to the bottom of who on the inside is trying to bring it all down.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“This should be a pleasant little interview. All I have to do is put on my scary face."<br />"You have a scary face?" Ingrid sounded skeptical.<br />"Yes," said Myfanwy indignantly. "I have a very scary face."<br />Ingrid surveyed her for a moment. "You may wish to take off the cardigan then, Rook Thomas," she advised tactfully. "The flowers on the pocket detract somewhat from your menace.” </i>
</blockquote><br />SO IN CONCLUSION: If you are looking for something with a solid premise the has some new takes on lore, mythology and such and doesn’t really have any romance looming in the wings than this might be for you. I enjoyed all the extras we get from Thomas as she tried to lead her new self after the amnesia creates a new person in her body and I’m pretty interested in seeing what becomes of Myfanwy in the future.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9968055385457948612" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2000835113" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2000835113" />
    <a title="Ginger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14097149-ginger"><img alt="Ginger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593449448p2/14097149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2000835113?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ginger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ginger" href="/user/show/14097149-ginger">Ginger</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14097149-ginger?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14097149-ginger?shelf=library-book">library-book</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2000835113" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9617850937228259210">I can’t believe this book has been under the radar for so long. Why haven’t more people read this duology? It’s a crying shame!<br/><br/>It starts off with a bang with the first line in the book. A fantastic way to start in my opinion.<br/><br/> <b>"Dear You,</b><br/> <b>The body you are wearing used to be mine."</b><br/><br/>Myfanwy Thomas wakes up surrounded by dead people that are wearing rubber gloves and has no idea who she is. The lucky thing about the plot is you’ll find out who she is, who she works for (a paranormal MI5) and why this </span>
  <span id="freeText9617850937228259210" style="display:none">I can’t believe this book has been under the radar for so long. Why haven’t more people read this duology? It’s a crying shame!<br /><br />It starts off with a bang with the first line in the book. A fantastic way to start in my opinion.<br /><br /> <b>"Dear You,</b><br /> <b>The body you are wearing used to be mine."</b><br /><br />Myfanwy Thomas wakes up surrounded by dead people that are wearing rubber gloves and has no idea who she is. The lucky thing about the plot is you’ll find out who she is, who she works for (a paranormal MI5) and why this has happened to her. She writes letters to herself before her memory is gone.<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10836728.The_Rook__The_Checquy_Files___1_" title="The Rook (The Checquy Files, #1) by Daniel O'Malley" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rook</a> has an interesting and original plot. The traitors in the organization were thought out and it was a complex plot.<br /><br /><b>The great parts about this book are as follows:</b><br /><br />A well-executed amnesia premise<br />A fun book about a supernatural secret agency<br />No romance that’s forced or otherwise in the book!<br />Cool characters that have supernatural abilities (think X-Men)<br />The writing was well done with plenty of snark and wit thrown in the mix.<br />The main characters were interesting and developed.<br /><br /><b>The parts that I had an issue with (not many):</b><br /><br />The pacing of the book. Felt a bit too long to me with more filler than is needed.<br />The ended was wrapped up to nicely for me with The Grafters. I’ve heard that the second book has a point of view with The Grafters. So, if that’s the case, maybe this won’t be an issue with me.<br /><br />I originally gave this 4 stars but I’m bumping it up to 4.5 stars because of the original plot!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2938575811" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2938575811" />
    <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten"><img alt="Jeffrey Keeten" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301087352p2/3427339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2938575811?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeffrey Keeten" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten">Jeffrey Keeten</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12988330-the-rook">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427339-jeffrey-keeten?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427339-jeffrey-keeten?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2938575811" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11354586094398615636"><b>“‘You,’ he said. ‘Your memories will be taken. They’ll be licked out of you, everything that makes you who you are. Gone forever. You’ll flee to a park, and there, in the rain, someone new will open the eyes that used to be yours.’ He spoke in a voice that cracked, and I stared at him in horror. “‘They’ll open your eyes, your black eyes, and see corpses all around them. Corpses wearing gloves.’”</b><br/><br/><a href='https://s1183.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/The%20Rook_zpsugmrp5lc.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1566864271i/28055669._SY540_.jpg' alt=' photo The Rook_zpsugmrp5lc.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>It is always unsettling when one receives portends of doom and gloom, but to have them related to </span>
  <span id="freeText11354586094398615636" style="display:none"><b>“‘You,’ he said. ‘Your memories will be taken. They’ll be licked out of you, everything that makes you who you are. Gone forever. You’ll flee to a park, and there, in the rain, someone new will open the eyes that used to be yours.’ He spoke in a voice that cracked, and I stared at him in horror. “‘They’ll open your eyes, your black eyes, and see corpses all around them. Corpses wearing gloves.’”</b><br><br><a href="https://s1183.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/The%20Rook_zpsugmrp5lc.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1566864271i/28055669._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo The Rook_zpsugmrp5lc.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>It is always unsettling when one receives portends of doom and gloom, but to have them related to you by a homeless person in the street somehow adds even more terror to any unsolicited foreshadowing of your future. He doesn’t know you, but he KNOWS what is going to happen to you, and given the other ominous signs you have received,...you have to believe him. <br><br>Her name is Myfanwy Alice Thomas. Don’t worry about the unfamiliar first name; she will instruct you on how she wants it pronounced. You are going to be dropped into the middle of dire circumstances. You are not going to know what is going on. There is a simple explanation for this. Your protagonist is going to be as clueless as you are. You are going to have to discover what the hell is going on together. <br><br>It doesn’t help that Myfanwy isn’t really Myfanwy. <i>”Who knew it would be so horrendously complicated impersonating oneself?”</i> It is certainly inconvenient to have people wanting to kill you. You didn’t do anything to anyone, but certainly the host of this body you are occupying obviously pissed off someone who feels the only solution to your disagreement is termination. You also have secret powers that are mostly unfathomable. You are a Rook in a secret organization, but what could that mean, and what is this clandestine group you work for? Certainly, it is helpful that the original Myfanwy left some notes. <br><br><b>”So, I suppose you’re wondering all about the Checquy Group. Oh, and please note that it is pronounced Sheck-Eh. French influences, I think. Or possibly just warped by generations of employees mispronouncing it. Don’t worry if the name means nothing to you. Most people never hear of it at all, but it has been in existence for centuries. It worked closely with the House of York, tended to ignore the Tudors, and endured the House of Stuart. However, it does not really matter who is ruling—from the earliest days, the organization’s loyalty has been to Britain rather than to a particular ruler.”</b><br><br>I have to laugh because I tend to ignore the Tudors as well. Some might even say I loathe those bastard usurpers, but really I shouldn’t let something that happened in 1485 on Bosworth Field, the end of a dynasty that I just happen to be related to, bother me in 2019. That would be ridiculous. <br><br>So what exactly do the Checquy do? They look into anything supernatural that needs to be contained and properly hidden from the public. Normal people must be allowed to go about their lives, unmolested by malevolent beings or even allowed to know such entities really exist. <i>”And here I am, on the way to Bath, to observe the chanting house that eats people.”</i> As an example of controlling information with misinformation, the chanting house that has been turned into a crater is released to the public as a gas leak explosion. <br><br>So Myfanwy must learn very quickly who she is, what she does, who she can trust, and who erased her memories. <br><br>I really enjoy the discombobulation. Daniel O’Malley has the reader feeling as if he has been caught wrong footed for a good portion of the novel. The notes left to the new Myfanwy are helpful and gives her and us enough information to keep us in the game. We are left in a constant state of thirsting for more revelations. I find myself endlessly speculating about what I do know exactly means. I am also worrying about how much highly essential information I am missing. The suspense keeps me reading feverishly to get the answers I am seeking. Starz has just released a TV series based on the books. I am looking forward to seeing how they portray the supernatural elements and also how they choose to dole out the information to the watcher. <br><br>If you wish to see more of my most recent book and movie reviews, visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jeffreykeeten.com">http://www.jeffreykeeten.com</a><br>I also have a Facebook blogger page at:<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/JeffreyKeeten">https://www.facebook.com/JeffreyKeeten</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11354586094398615636" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
